<p>The <b>Suriname national football team</b>  (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">Surinaams voetbalelftal</i>; <a href="/wiki/Sranan_Tongo" title="Sranan Tongo">Sranan Tongo</a>: <i>Sranankondre fubal pluga</i>) represent <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> in international football. It is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Surinamese_Football_Association" title="Surinamese Football Association">Surinamese Football Association</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Although the former <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colony</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, it competes in <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF" title="CONCACAF">CONCACAF</a>, together with <a href="/wiki/Guyana_national_football_team" title="Guyana national football team">Guyana</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana_national_football_team" title="French Guiana national football team">French Guiana</a>. Suriname was one of the founding members of CONCACAF in 1961. Suriname won the <a href="/wiki/CFU_Championship" title="CFU Championship">CFU Championship</a> in 1978, were runners-up in 1979 and have achieved three fourth place finishes in the CFU Championship/Caribbean Cup.
Suriname discourages dual citizenship and Surinamese-Dutch players who have picked up a Netherlands passport&#160;– which, crucially, offers legal work status in almost any European league&#160;– are barred from selection to the national team.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Many Suriname-born players and Dutch-born players of Surinamese descent, like <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Vanenburg" title="Gerald Vanenburg">Gerald Vanenburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruud_Gullit" title="Ruud Gullit">Ruud Gullit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Rijkaard" title="Frank Rijkaard">Frank Rijkaard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Davids" title="Edgar Davids">Edgar Davids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Seedorf" title="Clarence Seedorf">Clarence Seedorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Kluivert" title="Patrick Kluivert">Patrick Kluivert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Babel" title="Ryan Babel">Ryan Babel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aron_Winter" title="Aron Winter">Aron Winter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georginio_Wijnaldum" title="Georginio Wijnaldum">Georginio Wijnaldum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink" title="Jimmy Floyd Hasselbaink">Jimmy Floyd Hasselbaink</a> and  <a href="/wiki/Jeremain_Lens" title="Jeremain Lens">Jeremain Lens</a> have turned out to play for the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Dutch national team</a>. In 1999, <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_Mijnals" title="Humphrey Mijnals">Humphrey Mijnals</a>, who played for both Suriname and the Netherlands, was elected Surinamese footballer of the century.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Another famous player is <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Kamperveen" title="André Kamperveen">André Kamperveen</a>, who captained Suriname in the 1940s and was the first Surinamese to play professionally in the Netherlands.
</p><p>Suriname has participated in the qualifying matches for the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> since <a href="/wiki/1962_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1962 FIFA World Cup">1962</a>, but has never qualified for the finals. Suriname's strongest showing in World Cup qualification was the campaign for the <a href="/wiki/1978_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1978 FIFA World Cup">1978 finals</a>, when the national team reached the <a href="/wiki/1977_CONCACAF_Championship" title="1977 CONCACAF Championship">final group stage</a>.
</p><p>Suriname also came second in CONCACAF qualifying for the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1964_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 1964 Summer Olympics">1964 Olympics</a>, behind qualifiers <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a> and third in qualifying for the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1980_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 1980 Summer Olympics">1980 Olympics</a>, behind qualifiers <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica_national_football_team" title="Costa Rica national football team">Costa Rica</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men&#39;s national soccer team">United States</a>. The US then boycotted the Moscow Olympics, and were replaced by <a href="/wiki/Cuba_national_football_team" title="Cuba national football team">Cuba</a> in the football tournament, after Suriname opted to boycott the games as well.
</p><p>In 2008 Suriname advanced to the group stage of CONCACAF World Cup qualifying despite using only local players. With their two-leg victory over neighbours <a href="/wiki/Guyana_national_football_team" title="Guyana national football team">Guyana</a>, Suriname moved on to face <a href="/wiki/Haiti_national_football_team" title="Haiti national football team">Haiti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica_national_football_team" title="Costa Rica national football team">Costa Rica</a>, and <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador_national_football_team" title="El Salvador national football team">El Salvador</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_CONCACAF_Third_Round" title="2010 FIFA World Cup qualification – CONCACAF Third Round">third round</a>.
</p><p>Inspired by the success of teams with <a href="/wiki/FIFA_eligibility_rules" title="FIFA eligibility rules">dual nationals</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Algeria_at_the_FIFA_World_Cup" title="Algeria at the FIFA World Cup">Algeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surinamese_Football_Association" title="Surinamese Football Association">SVB</a> president John Krishnadath submitted a proposal to the national assembly to allow dual citizenship for athletes with the then-goal of reaching the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a> finals.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In order to support this project, a team with professional players of Surinamese origin was assembled and played an exhibition match on 26 December 2014 at the <a href="/wiki/Andre_Kamperveen_Stadion" class="mw-redirect" title="Andre Kamperveen Stadion">Andre Kamperveen Stadion</a>. The project is managed by <a href="/wiki/Nordin_Wooter" title="Nordin Wooter">Nordin Wooter</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Endt" title="David Endt">David Endt</a>, who have set up a presentation and sent invitations to 100 players of Surinamese origin, receiving 85 positive answers. <a href="/wiki/Dean_Gorr%C3%A9" title="Dean Gorré">Dean Gorré</a> was named to coach this special selection. <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> supported the project and granted insurance for the players and clubs despite the match being unofficial.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of May 2015, Gorré was the national team coach who oversaw both the official and unofficial teams. The professional team consisted of players willing to commit to Suriname if the dual-citizenship bill was approved, and played two international matches. In 2016, <a href="/wiki/Roberto_G%C3%B6deken" title="Roberto Gödeken">Roberto Gödeken</a> became the head coach once again. In <a href="/wiki/2017_Caribbean_Cup_qualification" title="2017 Caribbean Cup qualification">qualification for the 2017 Caribbean Cup</a>, Suriname secured a spot in the third round, but finished second behind <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_national_football_team" title="Jamaica national football team">Jamaica</a> in their group. However, as one of the three best second place finishers, Suriname advanced to face <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_national_football_team" title="Trinidad and Tobago national football team">Trinidad and Tobago</a> and Haiti in the 5th place play-off. Suriname won the match against Trinidad and Tobago, but lost against Haiti, and therefore once again failed to make an appearance in the Concacaf Gold Cup.
</p><p>In 2018 <a href="/wiki/Dean_Gorr%C3%A9" title="Dean Gorré">Dean Gorré</a> signed a new 2 year contract with the SVB to manage Natio once more. His first game ended in a draw against <a href="/wiki/Dominica_national_football_team" title="Dominica national football team">Dominica</a> in Nations League qualifiers. Gorré became not only the head coach of the senior team, but also overseas the youth teams and also has a helping hand in the introduction of a professional league in the country. Gorré also managed to arrange trainingcamps for the national team in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, where Natio have test their strength against professional and amateur football clubs.
</p><p>Suriname qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_CONCACAF_Nations_League_B" title="2019–20 CONCACAF Nations League B">CONCACAF Nations League B</a> after wins against <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_national_football_team" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis national football team">Saint Kitts and Nevis</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands_national_football_team" title="British Virgin Islands national football team">British Virgin Islands</a>, draw against Dominica and a loss against <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_national_football_team" title="Jamaica national football team">Jamaica</a>. Suriname got to share a group with <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua_national_football_team" title="Nicaragua national football team">Nicaragua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_national_football_team" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines national football team">SVG</a> and Dominica. After a narrow away win against Dominica, Suriname got to bag a massive 6-0 win at home against Nicaragua.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Competitive_record">Competitive record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Competitive record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl><dd><i>This is a list of honours for the senior Surinamese national team</i></dd></dl>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/CONCACAF_Championship" title="CONCACAF Championship">CONCACAF Championship</a> / <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF_Gold_Cup" title="CONCACAF Gold Cup">Gold Cup</a>:</b>
<ul><li>6th place: <a href="/wiki/1977_CONCACAF_Championship" title="1977 CONCACAF Championship">1977</a></li></ul></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/CCCF_Championship" title="CCCF Championship">CCCF Championship</a>:</b>
<ul><li>4th place: <a href="/wiki/1960_CCCF_Championship" title="1960 CCCF Championship">1960</a></li></ul></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/CFU_Championship" title="CFU Championship">CFU Championship</a> / <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Cup" title="Caribbean Cup">Caribbean Cup</a>:</b>
<ul><li><b>Winners</b>: <a href="/wiki/1978_CFU_Championship" title="1978 CFU Championship">1978</a></li>
<li>Runners-up: <a href="/wiki/1979_CFU_Championship" title="1979 CFU Championship">1979</a></li>
<li>4th place: <a href="/wiki/1994_Caribbean_Cup" title="1994 Caribbean Cup">1994</a>, <a href="/wiki/1996_Caribbean_Cup" title="1996 Caribbean Cup">1996</a></li></ul></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_Tournaments">Other Tournaments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Other Tournaments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/ABCS_Tournament" title="ABCS Tournament">ABCS Tournament</a></b>
<ul><li><b>Winners:</b> 2010, 2013, 2015</li>
<li>Runners-up: 2012</li>
<li>Third place: 2011</li></ul></li>
<li><b>Betty Brown Challenge Cup</b>
<ul><li><b>Winners:</b> 1943</li></ul></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/1966_Coupe_Duvalier" title="1966 Coupe Duvalier">Coupe Duvalier</a></b>
<ul><li>Runners-up: 1966</li></ul></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Parbo_Bier_Cup" title="Parbo Bier Cup">Parbo Bier Cup</a></b>
<ul><li>Runners-up: 2004</li></ul></li></ul>
